<div id="review_665258572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/665258572" />
    <a title="Arah-Lynda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda"><img alt="Arah-Lynda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601299926p2/5859453.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/665258572?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arah-Lynda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arah-Lynda" href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda">Arah-Lynda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481983556" href="/book/show/17373706-shift">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5859453-arah-lynda?shelf=i-said">i-said</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer665258572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15833259999777763256">The Shift is comprised of three parts: Legacy, Order and Pact, which if you have read Wool, promises answers to some of your questions.<br/><br/> I have read some complaints that the characters in The Shift were too flat, not fleshed out enough to become invested in. It is true that some of these characters did come across as mere shadows but I cannot help but get the sense that maybe that was the point.<br/><br/>In brief, <b>Legacy</b> tells us about what is happening in the world prior to the destruction we have seen an</span>
  <span id="freeText15833259999777763256" style="display:none">The Shift is comprised of three parts: Legacy, Order and Pact, which if you have read Wool, promises answers to some of your questions.<br /><br /> I have read some complaints that the characters in The Shift were too flat, not fleshed out enough to become invested in. It is true that some of these characters did come across as mere shadows but I cannot help but get the sense that maybe that was the point.<br /><br />In brief, <b>Legacy</b> tells us about what is happening in the world prior to the destruction we have seen and know from Wool. It introduces us to the players, takes us inside their thoughts and doubts and dreams, well at least those of Donald. From the other major players what we see primarily is manipulation of the weaker, more reliant members of the party; those that are indebted to the manipulators, for their positions and opportunities provided. A glimpse, if you will, of what life had been, a sneak peek at some of the doubts beginning to infiltrate the minds of the manipulated and a front row view into the minds of those in charge. Or is it?<br /><br />The <b>Order</b> tells us what life is like on the other side of that mirror of doubt. Here in silo 1 is where the main players come across as one dimensional, mere shadows; more like marionettes dancing to a tune orchestrated by others. Their purpose and their duty is all laid out for them, all they need do is comply and follow the rules, maintain order, until they can once again escape to the blissful void. Shift over. But first let’s take a peek outside…………<br /><br />Throughout The Shift time moves back and forth. We see life before the big catastrophic event, life shortly after, and life many years into the future. It is in the future that we meet new people, living their lives in other silos, engineered by those original members of The Legacy. I really liked Mission and found myself cheering for him, but it was The Crow that truly captured my imagination reminding me of The Oracle from the Matrix. These people and more living their lives unaware that manipulation and control are afoot; unaware that they are merely puppets, dancing on a string. <br /><br /><br />The <b>Pact</b> comprises the rules that everyone not charged with maintaining order, live by. We visit silo 17 and meet Jimmy. We learn what happened to his parents and all the others and while this was interesting I confess I did not need to read about his isolation, his fears, his scavenging and mind melting loneliness, page after page, through all those years. I got it long before I stopped reading about it. <br />But back in Silo 1 Donald’s mind is beginning to thaw, things are unravelling, a new plan is emerging………………………<br /><br /><br />While this is not the adrenaline paced, thumb sweating read that Wool was, Howey’s world is still extremely well imagined. The Shift answered many of the questions I had and gave birth to scads more.<br /><br /> <br />Count me in for Dust.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15833259999777763256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_670254171" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/670254171" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2067226-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1261147560p2/2067226.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/670254171?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/2067226-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer670254171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4572175309864681181">While I enjoyed Wool, this prequel left me cold for a number of reasons. First, there was the protagonist, Donald, whom everyone seems to value so highly but who never seems to do very much. One of Wool's strength's was that its mechanic thought like a mechanic, fixed things, and took action. Donald, as both architect and congressman, seems rarely to think like either, with his main action being going with the flow while wondering what is really going on.<br/><br/>I suppose if you're big conspiracy buff, </span>
  <span id="freeText4572175309864681181" style="display:none">While I enjoyed Wool, this prequel left me cold for a number of reasons. First, there was the protagonist, Donald, whom everyone seems to value so highly but who never seems to do very much. One of Wool's strength's was that its mechanic thought like a mechanic, fixed things, and took action. Donald, as both architect and congressman, seems rarely to think like either, with his main action being going with the flow while wondering what is really going on.<br /><br />I suppose if you're big conspiracy buff, that can make for a compelling narrative, but I'm not and it didn't for me. <br /><br />Shift's main characters -- Donald, Thurman, Anna, Mick -- act more like a high school clique than a bunch of people in government.<br /><br />First Shift is set in 2049, but it feels more like 2000. The global villains are still Iran and North Korea. Anna crawls under Donald's desk to install a new computer. The computer technology of Howey's future seems to have calcified in some pre-touchscreen era, and remains unconvincing. Social media seems non-existent. By 2049, no one uses Twitter or any kind of replacement. <br /><br />A small segment of society undertakes what is a difficult experiment -- setting up self-sustaining silo habitats -- a real technical challenge. This would have been fascinating to read about. But instead the book is mostly structured as a repeat of Wool's conspiracy tropes. Those worked well in Wool, when this society has been running for centuries. But here, where the very engineers and support crews running the whole thing take daily amnesia drugs -- which somehow let them selectively forget their past, their acquaintances, but not their job skills -- well, it just left me smacking my forehead, especially when used to justify an impersonation. Because these people who think through all forward consequences would never foresee that being a problem with their amnesia pills, when a simple photo ID would solve the problem.<br /><br />Additionally, Donald continually gets awakened to solve rebellion problems in other silos but then does very little to solve them, instead spending his time moping around trying to uncover "the truth." And to this reader, at least, the rebellion narratives in the other silos merely repeated the much stronger realization of rebellion in Wool. <br /><br />So, to sum up, if you really love conspiracy narrative, such as the never-ending later season conspiracies of something like the X-files, and repeats of Wool-like rebellion sequences, you might like this. But if you want a convincing origin story for the silos, you may be sadly disappointed. I actually wish I hadn't read this one, as it also diminished my opinion of Wool by the end. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4572175309864681181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_611487226" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/611487226" />
    <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy"><img alt="Jenny (Reading Envy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455391853p2/68030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/611487226?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny (Reading Envy)" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy">Jenny (Reading Envy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/17993080-shift">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=post-apocalypse-and-dystopia">post-apocalypse-and-dystopia</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read2014">read2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer611487226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15455315108612939166">I got this in audio because the third book in Silo was BOGO on Audible, and now I'm not sure I care to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17855756.Dust__Wool___9___Silo___3_' title='Dust (Wool, #9) (Silo, #3) by Hugh Howey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dust (Wool, #9)</a>. I loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13453029.Wool_Omnibus__Silo___1___Wool___1_5_' title='Wool Omnibus (Silo, #1) (Wool, #1-5) by Hugh Howey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wool Omnibus (Silo, #1)</a> and thought I would be interested in reading the prequel, the "how it all happened in the first place" story, but in the end, not so much. I actually think finding out the hows and whys do a disservice to the strange and isolated world we read about in Wool and I'm sorry I read this book. I'm even sorrier I spent so many hours listening to i</span>
  <span id="freeText15455315108612939166" style="display:none">I got this in audio because the third book in Silo was BOGO on Audible, and now I'm not sure I care to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17855756.Dust__Wool___9___Silo___3_" title="Dust (Wool, #9) (Silo, #3) by Hugh Howey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dust (Wool, #9)</a>. I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13453029.Wool_Omnibus__Silo___1___Wool___1_5_" title="Wool Omnibus (Silo, #1) (Wool, #1-5) by Hugh Howey" rel="nofollow noopener">Wool Omnibus (Silo, #1)</a> and thought I would be interested in reading the prequel, the "how it all happened in the first place" story, but in the end, not so much. I actually think finding out the hows and whys do a disservice to the strange and isolated world we read about in Wool and I'm sorry I read this book. I'm even sorrier I spent so many hours listening to it, although near the end it was at 2.5x speed just to get through it. <br /><br />I gave it 2 stars because there were a few highlights - the character of Jimmy, the child left to fend for himself, was interesting, although difficult to write about. It actually might have been more interesting to focus on him in a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41667.My_Side_of_the_Mountain__Mountain___1_" title="My Side of the Mountain (Mountain, #1) by Jean Craighead George" rel="nofollow noopener">My Side of the Mountain</a> kind of treatment. The ending brought some things together kind of as a favor to those of us who finished. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15455315108612939166" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/715613331?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob Wheatley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob Wheatley" href="/user/show/10844435-rob-wheatley">Rob Wheatley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer715613331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4408492246255925240">Arggh!<br/><br/>I like the concept.<br/><br/>I wanted to find out what happens.<br/><br/>I hated the execution!<br/><br/><br/>I found myself screaming at this book. I really liked the idea and I really wanted to keep reading to find out how it all ends, but I found aspects of the book really frustrating. You'll find yourself saying "for god's sake, just get on with it will you" and "Well, that doesn't fit" all the way through this book. If you can put up with that, then it's worth the read.<br/><br/>Spoiler alert - don't read any more if you haven't</span>
  <span id="freeText4408492246255925240" style="display:none">Arggh!<br /><br />I like the concept.<br /><br />I wanted to find out what happens.<br /><br />I hated the execution!<br /><br /><br />I found myself screaming at this book. I really liked the idea and I really wanted to keep reading to find out how it all ends, but I found aspects of the book really frustrating. You'll find yourself saying "for god's sake, just get on with it will you" and "Well, that doesn't fit" all the way through this book. If you can put up with that, then it's worth the read.<br /><br />Spoiler alert - don't read any more if you haven't read this book yet:<br /><br />For instance.<br /><br />- How do children's books last 100s of years of use?<br /><br />- Why have children's books with pictures of the outside world (grass, sky, animals etc) if you are trying to hide this from the silo occupants?<br /><br />- Why do 'regular' people in regular silos have tins of food (Jimmy looking for a can opener and finding canned food). More to the point, why have canned cat food that's edible 100s of years after the occupation of the silo. Come to think of it, why are there cats there in the 1st place give the way the silos we occupied!?!?!<br /><br />- Why didn't Donald piece it all together in the 2 years he was given The Order to read, or at least ask a couple of questions<br /><br />Other things are frustrating too, like the long pointless dialogues (e.g. between Donald and his wife).<br /><br />It was things like this that got me frustrated, but at the same time I wanted to read on...... </span>
  <a data-text-id="4408492246255925240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_648600620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648600620" />
    <a title="Jon Swartz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13359689-jon-swartz"><img alt="Jon Swartz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448908075p2/13359689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/648600620?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon Swartz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon Swartz" href="/user/show/13359689-jon-swartz">Jon Swartz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer648600620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3116755742167985653">I assumed it wouldn't be possible for Hugh Howey to match the suspense and freshness of the first of this series, Wool, but he surprised me. Shift is both a prequel and a companion novel, showing the ingenuous origins of the strange claustrophobic Wool universe, then moving forward to follow parallel characters and locations that we glimpsed only briefly in Wool. As before the action weaves between several different story lines and times, each told from the point of view of a different full fles</span>
  <span id="freeText3116755742167985653" style="display:none">I assumed it wouldn't be possible for Hugh Howey to match the suspense and freshness of the first of this series, Wool, but he surprised me. Shift is both a prequel and a companion novel, showing the ingenuous origins of the strange claustrophobic Wool universe, then moving forward to follow parallel characters and locations that we glimpsed only briefly in Wool. As before the action weaves between several different story lines and times, each told from the point of view of a different full fleshed character.<br /><br />Shift and Wool remind me a bit of the TV series Lost -- the self-contained world and its mysteries slowly unraveled -- but where Lost just piled on mysteries with no intention of answering them, these books wrap up satisfyingly.<br /><br />No idea if there's going to be a third installment, and once again I can't imagine how the same freshness could be generated, but this time around I won't be as surprised if he does!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3116755742167985653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_912718947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/912718947" />
    <a title="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady"><img alt="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601761303p2/22943325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/912718947?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" href="/user/show/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady">Maxine (Booklover Catlady)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781780891217" href="/book/show/17307612-shift">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer912718947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5416319870906283654">I simply couldn't finish this, it seemed to go on and on and on with over descriptive paragraphs and pages of nothingness.<br/><br/>I didn't realise Shift was the prequel to the Wool Omnibus, I had loved Wool and wanted to know what was next instead I was plummeted into the "before". But it was tedious reading, I lasted 250 pages and just had to stop. I skipped to the last few chapters and have the feeling I didn't miss much in between.<br/><br/>What a shame that the books didn't move forward in time, I found the c</span>
  <span id="freeText5416319870906283654" style="display:none">I simply couldn't finish this, it seemed to go on and on and on with over descriptive paragraphs and pages of nothingness.<br /><br />I didn't realise Shift was the prequel to the Wool Omnibus, I had loved Wool and wanted to know what was next instead I was plummeted into the "before". But it was tedious reading, I lasted 250 pages and just had to stop. I skipped to the last few chapters and have the feeling I didn't miss much in between.<br /><br />What a shame that the books didn't move forward in time, I found the characters in this so one dimensional and lacking in density of character, and things just blurred into never-ending words. I struggled to picture what was going on in my minds eye.<br /><br />I'm gutted! I had such high hopes, this was just too wordy and perhaps not so clever going back on the timeline rather than forwards. I'm unsure if I will read the last Omnibus "Dust" now. Really disappointed and I tried so hard to love it as I did Wool.<br /><br />I need a strong coffee now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5416319870906283654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2794605053" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2794605053" />
    <a title="Tracy Robinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63306072-tracy-robinson"><img alt="Tracy Robinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530821374p2/63306072.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2794605053?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracy Robinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracy Robinson" href="/user/show/63306072-tracy-robinson">Tracy Robinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481983556" href="/book/show/17373706-shift">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2794605053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14172514647547053273">I may write a longer review later, or “as way leads onto way”, I won’t because I’ve gotten tangled up in life stuff. <br/><br/>I read WOOL at the end of January and devoured it over the course of 6 hours or so. This one was paced out as I buddy read it with my pal Jen, and I was glad to have someone to talk with - to sort things out with. <br/><br/>This installment tells us the backstory of the world that came to be in WOOL. A pre-apocalypse, an apocalypse, and post apocalypse, if you will. As before, I love Howey’</span>
  <span id="freeText14172514647547053273" style="display:none">I may write a longer review later, or “as way leads onto way”, I won’t because I’ve gotten tangled up in life stuff. <br /><br />I read WOOL at the end of January and devoured it over the course of 6 hours or so. This one was paced out as I buddy read it with my pal Jen, and I was glad to have someone to talk with - to sort things out with. <br /><br />This installment tells us the backstory of the world that came to be in WOOL. A pre-apocalypse, an apocalypse, and post apocalypse, if you will. As before, I love Howey’s writing, characterization, and sense of suspense/pacing. It has science elements, but only what I need to know and I love that. <br /><br />Now I am reaching for the final book but I DO NOT HAVE IT. This needs to be rectified. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14172514647547053273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2036886246" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2036886246" />
    <a title="Althea Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann"><img alt="Althea Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411566466p2/3846743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2036886246?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Althea Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Althea Ann" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann">Althea Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2036886246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1468907721745611578">Read this follow-up to "Wool" for post-apocalyptic book club. <br/><br/>'Shift' contains three parts, 'Legacy,' 'Order,' and 'Pact.' Each is also available as a separate publication, but I recommend the omnibus edition. I also recommend reading 'Wool' first, even though the events here precede it chronologically. If you've read 'Wool' you know the scenario: survivors of a mysterious apocalypse living in massive underground silos, struggling to survive in the face of social oppression, dwindling resources </span>
  <span id="freeText1468907721745611578" style="display:none">Read this follow-up to "Wool" for post-apocalyptic book club. <br /><br />'Shift' contains three parts, 'Legacy,' 'Order,' and 'Pact.' Each is also available as a separate publication, but I recommend the omnibus edition. I also recommend reading 'Wool' first, even though the events here precede it chronologically. If you've read 'Wool' you know the scenario: survivors of a mysterious apocalypse living in massive underground silos, struggling to survive in the face of social oppression, dwindling resources and mechanical decay. In 'Shift,' we get to find out how it all happened.<br /><br />'First Shift - Legacy' shifts (haha) between two perspectives. In the near future, junior politician Donald (an unfortunately distracting choice of character name - who would've guessed?) is tasked by his mentor with work on a secret project. Donald was an architect before he went into politics, and Senator Thurman wants him to design a massive bomb shelter. The job takes him away from the side of his wife, and puts him into uncomfortable proximity to his college ex- (Thurman's daughter) - but he can't say no, as Thurman was responsible for getting Donald elected.<br />This story is intercut with a glimpse into the future world of the Silos. In Silo One, "Troy" awakes and is given the job of IT Supervisor. Troy is oddly unable to remember many things about his past, but he knows the scenario: the men of Silo One are responsible for overseeing all 50 silos. They wake for shifts of work, and after a few months, return to cryosleep. The situation is psychologically draining, and not everyone can hack it...<br />Of course, the reader knows that the two narratives must be connected, but it's a pleasure waiting for the pieces to match up.<br /><br />'Second Shift' also features two linked narratives. In one, we continue the drama in Silo One, between Donald, Senator Thurman, and his daughter, Anna, as Donald is awoken from cryosleep for his 'second shift.' In the other narrative, the action takes place in Silo 18, where we meet a young porter called Mission, who has never known any other world but that of his silo. The only inkling he and his contemporaries have had that things might once have been different are the stories of an elderly teacher, who tells fantastic tales - tales that seem unlikely, but at the same time, are sufficient to sow the seeds of discontent. And the society of Silo 18 may be increasingly unstable...<br /><br />'Third Shift' - two more stories. Due to an error (or is it?) when Donald is awoken for his third shift, he is mistaken for Senator Thurman. As long as no one finds out; he'll stay in charge of the whole shebang. Will this give Donald a chance to redeem himself for his part in the destruction of the world? Or will he continue to make yet more mistakes and stupid decisions?<br />In the second story, we go back and explore the 'origin story' of the character of Jimmy/Solo, who will be familiar to readers of 'Wool.' Let's just say that when you're a nerdy kid whose survival depends on hiding from and if necessary, shooting every other survivor you encounter, cause they're all out to kill you, the psychological result is not ideal. <br /><br />Because Jimmy's story relies on the linkage back to 'Wool,' on its own, it might be the weakest of the three. And, to a degree, I did feel that 'Shift' was written as an afterthought, and in response to the runaway popularity of 'Wool.' Some of the ideas seem a bit reverse-engineered, as far as how everything in the silos works and why decisions were made the way they were. It's still engagingly written - it's a long book, but moves along quite quickly, not inviting too much detailed analysis of the nitty-gritty specifics. Overall - not quite as good as 'Wool,' but it still squeaks up to 4 stars, for me. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1468907721745611578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Here it goes:<br><br>"I am afraid of" List (in order of whatever):<br>1. That there will be more Twilight and Fifty Shades of Gray books. <br>2. That I will never meet my Mr. Rochester. <br>3. Apocalypse where everybody is living underground. <br>4. Heights. <br>5. That G.R.R.Martin will never finish "The Game Of Thrones". <br>6. That Hogwarts doesn't exist. <br>7. (To Be Filled)<br>9. The person who took number 8. <br>10. (To Be Filled)<br><br>Comparing my list to the "Fears of 2015", my list is not that impressive. SIGHT. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471626190i/20082964._SX540_.jpg" width="650" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Going back to "Shift" - it wasn't impressive. In TV world such book would have been called "a filler" - an episode that explains a lot, but well, is kinda boring and gives not much about what to expect further. If this was the first book of the series, I doubt if I would have read further. It has the same feeling of darkness, suffocation and mystery as the first book, but it's not shocking, different or awesome. It's like reading a washing machine manual when you already centrifuged your cat. Howey has it's own unique style and "digs deep", but I would have rather read the explanation of creation of silos incorporated in further stories than taking a step back and reading a prequel. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471626640ra/20083006.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And, ummm... What book is next in the series? The order of Howey books is a mind-fuck... </span>
  <a data-text-id="15399679765518113615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('S2v7bn87F1ULxxJwbnlMrqt64mmUeRGZREJDjZpX/h0zU9zDgq8bUgEF3Xv3HxWLyVi5lDdNnx6vO8vrxNxY1g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CDioED0FNPyAlN97Q4W4vhOHZ7J4/krLIPlN1AcYYU1wAI+9wJE4+4pWEHDa4+GbcaU8T9vKxEzLgMWyWZPHhg==')})
  }

But it’s getting harder not to fight back and earn yet another strike tattoo on her neck.\n\nEverything changes one ordinary day watching the latest catch of smugglers and Strikers being returned for justice.
